In addition, younger workers have greatly different attitudes towards their careers and their expectations of work than previous generations.\nThis complex and changing dynamic presents significant challenges for employers to manage health and safety, while also meeting operational requirements and maintaining a positive workplace culture.\nWorkshop Objectives & Key Outcomes\nP2 Group has developed our Human Maintenance Schedule methodology that aligns the performance of people with the demands of the role, and ensures that organisations are ready to manage the challenges and opportunities that are presented by an aging workforce.\nThe Managing an Ageing Workforce Workshop provides an overview of this approach and aims to up-skill executives, managers, and supervisors in managing the workplace health and wellbeing of their workforce.\nTaking an interactive approach, P2 Group focus on a range of practical case studies, skills building activities, and the provision of effective workplace tools to ensure that organisations are equipped to best address the diverse health and wellbeing needs of workers.\nOver the course of workshop P2 Group will up-skill managers in:\n\nRecognising the different needs and challenges experienced by workers throughout the spectrum of their working life\nUnderstanding an employer\u2019s legal obligations in the health and wellbeing space\nIdentifying the early warning signs of physical and psychological conditions\nDeveloping strategies for assisting workers with their health and wellbeing and implementing a uniform workplace policy\nUnderstanding the importance of a human maintenance schedule based upon workability\nConsidering reasonable adjustments and flexible working arrangements\nUtilising the inherent requirements of job as a workforce management strategy.\n\n",

Where is the best place for you to invest your precious time?\r\nThe first question to ask is, \"Are we grant ready?\". Many organisations fail in their applications due to a lack of preparation, project clarity, sustainable outcomes and partners? Most funders have different requirements and application processes. This session will help to set up a framework from which your organisation can be ready to apply for any grant efficiently and effectively.\r\nThis session is designed for grant writers with limited experience in writing grants for non-profit organisations.\r\nWhat you will learn\r\nFollowing the workshop, you will be able to:\r\n\r\nRecognise what grants are most suitable for your organisation and where to find them\r\nSell your organisation and the project / program\r\nDefine the project / program and its benefits\r\nCalculate the cost of the plan and prepare a budget\r\nDetermine who are important stakeholders and partners\r\nUnderstand sustainability, and how to keep the project / program going after funding finishes\r\nGive thanks!\r\n\r\nWhat involved?\r\nThis session will assist your grant writers and fundraising committees to understand the broader picture of grant giving and provide a base for applying for a range of grants for your organisation.\r\nWho should attend?\r\nAnyone who is involved, or has input in writing grants for their organisation such as Board and committee members, fundraising committees, staff and volunteers.\r\n\u00a0\r\nProgram Details\r\nDate:\u00a0Tuesday 25 June, 2019\r\nTime:\u00a09.30am - 4.30pm\r\nLocation:\u00a0Ross House Association, 247 - 251 Flinders Lane, Melbourne, Victoria, 3000\r\n\r\nContact:\u00a01300 144 113 or debbie@nonprofittraining.com.au\r\n",
